Knrr BnowN
Covernor

ORDER ON REMISSION  OF FINES PURSUANT  TO ARTICLE  V,
SECTION  14 OF THE OREGON  CONSTITUTION
(Circuit Court Cases)

WHEREAS,  until recently, courts regularly  suspended driver  licenses  for nonpayment  of
traffic fines,  without  any inquiry into the financial  circumstances of the driver  or their
ability to pay.

WHEREAS,  the loss of a license  thrusts low-income  Oregonians  into a court debt spiral
because  they  often continue  to rack up additional fines  for driving with a suspended
license  to obtain  goods and  services  to meet their basic  needs, and they are less likely  to
get or keep  a job to pay these fines without  a license.

WHEREAS,  with the passage  of HB 4210 in2020,  the legislature  acknowledged  that
this  is bad public  policy that disproportionately  impacts  low-income  Oregonians  and
people  of color.

WHEREAS,  unfortunately.  while HB 4210 repealed  debt-based  license suspensions  in
Oregon, it left existing  nonpayment-related  license suspensions  in place-and  those
suspensions  last l0 to 20 years.

WHEREAS,  as a result,  thousands  of Oregonians remain  burdened by these  legacy
suspensions  of their driver  licenses  that are no longer  allowed under current Oregon law.

WHEREAS,  many  of these individuals  face  abject and crippling poverty that a driver
license  can help  them climb out of.

WHEREAS,  today, I am taking  steps  to alleviate  this burden and enable  thousands  of
Oregonians to seek reinstatement  of their driver  licenses  by clearing  the fines associated
with many of these unjust  legacy  suspensions,  which will, in tum, allow the associated
debt-based  suspensions  to be cleared.

WHEREAS,  I asked the Driver and Motor Vehicles  Division of ODOT  (DMV) to
provide  me a list of cases  that met the following  criteria:  (1) the affected  person received
a traffic violation, under state law, in Oregon;  (2) the affected person has  a driver  license
that is currently  suspended  or, due to the suspension,  has downgraded  to an ID card or
has a valid  hardship  permit;  (3) the only sanction preventing DMV from  reinstating  the
affected person's  driver license is a Failure  to Comply  or Failure  to Appear sanction
obtained in the underlying  traffic violation case;  (4) that sanction occurred  prior  to

254 STATE  CAPITOL, SALEM c,R 97BOr -4047 (5O3) 37a-Ar  r r  FAX (5O3) 37A-A97O
WvlIvl,.GOVE  R NOR.OR EGO N.GOV

ORDER ON REMISSION  OF FINES  PURSUANT  TO ARTICLE  V, SECTION  14
OF THE OREGON  CONSTITUTION
PAGE TWO

October  1,2020;and  (5) DMV  has an Oregon address for the affected  person and its
records  reflect that the affected  person is not deceased  (collectively the "Remission
Criteria").

WHEREAS,  each case  meeting  the Remission  Criteria  is listed in Exhibit A, attached
hereto  and incorporated  herein  by reference (collectively  the "Remission Cases"  and each
a "Remission Case").

WHEREAS,  each Remission  Case listed in Exhibit  A includes  fines  and  fees imposed on
the respective individual in that Remission  Case  (the "Court-Ordered  Fines and Fees").

WHEREAS,  the continued  burden that these Court-Ordered  Fines  and  Fees imposes  on
each  affected  individual in the Remission  Cases  does not serve the best  interests of the
State of Oregon or of those  individuals.

NOW  THEREFORE, by virtue  of the authority  vested  in me under Article  V, Section
14, of the Oregon Constitution,  I, Kate Brown,  Governor  of the State of Oregon, hereby:

l.  Remit all outstanding  Court-Ordered  Fines  and Fees  imposed by the

judgments listed in each Remission  Case, except  for any restitution  awards,  as
defined  in ORS 137.103(3),  and compensatory  fines,  as described in ORS
137.101; and

2. All outstanding  Court-Ordered  Fines  and Fees  imposed under the judgments
listed in this Remission  Order,  with the exception  of restitution  awards,  as
defined  in ORS 137.103(3),  and compensatory  fines,  as described in ORS
137.101, shall be considered paid in full and satisfied  as of the date of this
Remission  Order;  and

3. Notwithstanding  any of the above,  this Remission  Order  shall  not apply  to any

Remission  Case listed in Exhibit A for which the underlying  offense
associated  with that case number  is a misdemeanor  or felony,  as defined  in
ORS 161 .505  et seq.; and

4. This Remission  Order  does not create a right  of reimbursement  for any
affected  individuals  with a Remission  Case listed in Exhibit A; and

5. Nothing in this Remission  Order authorizes the affected  individuals  with
Remission  Cases  listed in Exhibit A to drive without first satisfying the
requirements  for a valid driver  license, registration, and insurance;  and

ORDER  ON REMISSION  OF FINES  PURSUANT  TO ARTICLE  V, SECTION  14
OF THE  OREGON  CONSTITUTION
PAGE THREE

6. I direct my staff  to provide copies, electronically  or otherwise,  of this

Remission  Order to the presiding judge of the court  that issued  each judgment
imposing Court-Ordered  Fines  and Fees that are remitted by this Remission
Order,  so that those  courts may  update  their records, promptly  provide the
DMV with  notice  to reinstate the affected  individual's  suspended  driving
privileges  as required  by ORS  809.220(3)(a)  and  ORS  809.130(2),  and take
such  other  steps  that are necessary to effectuate  this Remission  Order.

Done before me at Salem,  Oregon, this 2lst day of December,2022.

t*6u***

KATE BROWN

Identified Data Fields:

We have done our best to automaticly identify and name form fields according to our naming conventions. When possible, we've used names tied to our question library. See e.g., user1_name. If we think we've found a match to a question in our library, it is highlighted in green. Novel names are auto generated. So, you will probably need to edit some of them if you're trying to stick to the convention.
